## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core problem in materials science and solid mechanics. Stress typically increases with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), with various nonlinear coupling effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at small deformations)
- Thermal elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (combined linear and power-law hardening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (exponential saturation stress-strain curve)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (coupled strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1/T)) (thermally-activated flow stress)
- Linear thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with exponential thermal factor)
- Homologous temperature softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (power-law thermal softening)
- Sinh-based flow stress (Sellars-Tegart): sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (1/T))) (high-temperature creep/flow)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive model)
- Combined Voce + thermal: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal activation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperatures → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (Tm - T)**c or exp(-c*T) multiplying the mechanical response
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally-activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) reflecting activation energy barriers
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) separating initial yield from subsequent hardening
- Power-law creep coupling → sigma proportional to epsilon_dot**c1 * exp(c2/T), suggesting rate-temperature equivalence
- Multiplicative decomposition of thermal and mechanical effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable contributions
- Concave-up to concave-down transition in stress-strain → competing hardening (epsilon**c1) and dynamic recovery terms
- Hyperbolic sine flow law → sinh(c*sigma) appears in high-temperature deformation, invertible to arcsinh form for sigma
